## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: materials science / constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship of a material, a core problem in solid mechanics and materials science. Stress typically increases with strain (linearly in elastic regime, nonlinearly in plastic), while increasing temperature generally reduces stress through thermal softening of elastic modulus and yield strength.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elastic regime)
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus: sigma = c0 * (1 - c1 * T) * epsilon (linear elasticity with thermal softening)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (plastic strain hardening, Hollomon equation)
- Ramberg-Osgood type: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 + c1 * epsilon**c2) (combined elastic-plastic behavior)
- Johnson-Cook simplified: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - c3 * T**c4) (strain hardening with thermal softening)
- Arrhenius thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 / T) (thermally activated deformation)
- Voce hardening with temperature: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * epsilon)) * exp(c2 / T) (saturation hardening with thermal activation)
- Linear thermal softening with power hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 - T) (simple thermal softening model)
- Ludwik equation: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic-plastic with yield stress offset)
- Temperature-dependent Ludwik: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(-c3 * T) (Ludwik with exponential thermal softening)
- Swift hardening: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (shifted power law for pre-strained materials)
- Polynomial stress-strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (polynomial constitutive model)
- Hyperbolic sine flow stress: sigma = c0 * T * asinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 / T)) (Garofalo/Sellars-Tegart creep model)
- Combined model: sigma = c0 * epsilon / (1 + c1 * epsilon) * (1 - c2 * T) (saturation hardening with linear thermal softening)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening of elastic modulus → multiplicative factor (1 - c*T) or (c0 - T)**c1 or exp(-c*T) applied to stress
- Strain hardening saturation → Voce-type form (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) indicating dislocation density saturation
- Thermally activated dislocation motion → Arrhenius factor exp(c/T) or exp(-c*T) coupling temperature to flow stress
- Yield stress offset → additive constant c0 in stress (representing initial yield before hardening)
- Strain hardening exponent typically between 0 and 1 → power law epsilon**c with 0 < c < 1 for metals
- Phase transition or melting effects → stress approaching zero near a critical temperature, modeled as (c0 - T) terms
- Competing hardening and recovery → difference of exponentials or rational forms in strain
- Homologous temperature scaling → T appears normalized as c0*T rather than raw T in constitutive models
